<div id="review_1702198610" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1702198610" />
    <a title="Breinholt Dorrough" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54459790-breinholt-dorrough"><img alt="Breinholt Dorrough" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578449078p2/54459790.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1702198610?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Breinholt Dorrough" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Breinholt Dorrough" href="/user/show/54459790-breinholt-dorrough">Breinholt Dorrough</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780547572291" href="/book/show/12346742-ubik">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1702198610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2151464178977214993">While I was reading this book, a bomb exploded in my apartment, tearing my paperback copy of Ubik to pieces. The book had been badly burned and found itself in tatters. After placing it into a protective cooler packed with solid state carbon dioxide, I rushed to take it to a local book-shop (located next to the morgue) to see if there was any hope of putting the pages back together, or at least what was left of them, to be able to commune with it — my cherished, fragile half-book — every once in</span>
  <span id="freeText2151464178977214993" style="display:none">While I was reading this book, a bomb exploded in my apartment, tearing my paperback copy of Ubik to pieces. The book had been badly burned and found itself in tatters. After placing it into a protective cooler packed with solid state carbon dioxide, I rushed to take it to a local book-shop (located next to the morgue) to see if there was any hope of putting the pages back together, or at least what was left of them, to be able to commune with it — my cherished, fragile half-book — every once in a while, even though it was half-dead.<br /><br />However, after arriving at the book-shop, I was surprised to notice Philip K. Dick's face on my credit card. At first I was thinking his face was going to appear on the coins in my pocket, but then I remembered that in 2017 coins no longer exist in the United States.<br /><br />But then suddenly coins did exist. I felt them jingle right there in my pocket. It was impossible, I thought. I mean, who the hell uses coins anymore? That is when I started to think something had gone dreadfully wrong.<br /><br />I tried buying things with the coins to see if anything else had changed in my reality, but every store declined to accept them, and no ATM would receive them, given that they are no longer valid forms of currency. Sure, in 2017 we may not have spaceships or functional cryogenic freezing or time control powers or other cognitive abilities, but at least we don't run around carrying something as antiquated and useless as coins like they did in 1992. Could you imagine if you needed a nickel every time you needed to open your fridge door? You'd starve to death! I can't blame Joe for not having coins around. Useless devices.<br /><br />I had spent so much time ranting about how I suddenly had coins I couldn't use that I failed to notice how stale my cigarettes were. Wait a minute, now what the hell am I doing with cigarettes? I thought. I've never smoked a day in my life. How would I even know what a stale cigarette is?<br /><br />It's no matter, I thought. I decided to go back to Omaha, my birthplace, to watch the burial of my book. Then the girl who flashed me to get a job at the company (I really doubted she could see into the future, but as soon as she had removed her shirt of in front of me there was no doubt she could read my mind) told me she was the one who had burned my book. I became really upset with her, until she withered away and died. Then I felt bad. I mean, sure, she was jealous that I had slept with that other girl who didn't have to flash me to get the job, but that doesn't mean she was a bad person.<br /><br />I started feeling really sick and clambered up to my hotel room. Then my best buddy appeared and introduced me to spray paint. "Spray paint will solve all your problems when you're dead," he said. "Look!" He sprayed me with spray paint, and I recovered instantly. My friend added: "Oh, by the way, you're dead. That's why you can use spray paint. You can also use spray paint as deodorant or breakfast cereal, or any of the other advertised purposes found in your cherished bombed book. Spray paint is magical stuff. My dead wife invented it."<br /><br />Then I made the devil spray paint himself and I gained power over him.<br /><br />Moral of the story: SPRAY PAINT IS GOD<br /><br />Right now Philip K. Dick is crossing the River Styx with coins over his eyes, and those coins now have my face on them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2151464178977214993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1771099153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1771099153" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3144945-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594856152p2/3144945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1771099153?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/3144945-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/6000003-ubik">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3144945-alex?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1771099153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17897130964339159087">"Our own homegrown Borges" is how Ursula Le Guin describes Philip K. Dick, because they both use writing to question the nature of reality. Both writers assume that everything is up for debate: the story, the page it's written on, the author writing it. <br/><br/>Dick is my favorite of the pack of mid-century science fiction writers. (The "Big Three" of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/988919566' title='My review of Friday - I dislike Heinlein' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heinlein,</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1750088647' title='My review of I, Robot - I like Asimov' rel='nofollow noopener'>Asimov</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1743336231' title='my review of Rendezvous with Rama, which I like' rel='nofollow noopener'>Clarke,</a> plus <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/488675677' title='My review of Fahrenheit 451, which I hate' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bradbury,</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1101570720' title='My review of The Dispossessed - Le Guin is okay for me' rel='nofollow noopener'>Le Guin</a> and him.) He's best known as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7082.Do_Androids_Dream_of_Electric_Sheep_' title='Blade Runner etc.' rel='nofollow noopener'>a short story writer;</a> of his 44 novels, The Man in the High Castle is his</span>
  <span id="freeText17897130964339159087" style="display:none">"Our own homegrown Borges" is how Ursula Le Guin describes Philip K. Dick, because they both use writing to question the nature of reality. Both writers assume that everything is up for debate: the story, the page it's written on, the author writing it. <br><br>Dick is my favorite of the pack of mid-century science fiction writers. (The "Big Three" of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/988919566" title="My review of Friday - I dislike Heinlein" rel="nofollow noopener">Heinlein,</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1750088647" title="My review of I, Robot - I like Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Asimov</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1743336231" title="my review of Rendezvous with Rama, which I like" rel="nofollow noopener">Clarke,</a> plus <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/488675677" title="My review of Fahrenheit 451, which I hate" rel="nofollow noopener">Bradbury,</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1101570720" title="My review of The Dispossessed - Le Guin is okay for me" rel="nofollow noopener">Le Guin</a> and him.) He's best known as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7082.Do_Androids_Dream_of_Electric_Sheep_" title="Blade Runner etc." rel="nofollow noopener">a short story writer;</a> of his 44 novels, The Man in the High Castle is his most famous but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1061467324" title="My review" rel="nofollow noopener">it's pretty flawed,</a> so when Lev Grossman wants him represented on Time Magazine's top 100 novels of an arbitrary period, <a href="http://entertainment.time.com/2005/10/16/all-time-100-novels/slide/ubik-1969-by-philip-k-dick/" title="And here it is" rel="nofollow noopener"><i>Ubik</i> is up.</a><br><br>But who are the characters? What is the setting? Does anyone exist? What time is it? In 2016 I'm reading a book written in 1969, set in 1992, decaying to 1939. Here's a chart.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475500685i/20727141._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Here's what happens: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Joe Chip, his femme fatale Pat Conley, and their whole anti-psionic team are assassinated via bomb by the psi organization Hollis. They are all stashed in cryo sleep, where they can be somewhat communicated with by (among others) their employer and sole surviver Runciter. There they're ambushed by a powerful cryo sleeper named Jory, who manipulates their near-death dreams in order to swallow their souls. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Every chapter is basically a twist ending to the chapter before it - this book is like a series of trapdoors - and in the final twist, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Runciter realizes that he too is dead. They have perhaps all been invading each other's dreams. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Ubik - pronounced like "ubiquitous" - is slippery. Nostalgia is death, literally, and Ubik (in its MacGuffin form, as an aerosol spray) is the new, which might save you - at least temporarily. But why the cynical ads for Ubik products at the top of each chapter? That implies that it's rotten itself. It doesn't seem to work very well, anyway.<br><br><a href="http://www.deviantart.com/art/GET-SOME-UBIK-384571012" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475500685i/20727142._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This is anticlimactic if you try too hard to explain it. The answer isn't the answer; the question is the answer. (Whee!) It's fun to wrestle all this out, but there's no explanation that totally satisfies. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1469344209" title="My review of The Castle" rel="nofollow noopener">Like Kafka,</a> Dick isn't trying to write something that makes <i>sense.</i> He's trying to point out that nothing makes sense. Reality is subjective and you will never be sure that the one you experience is "real."<br><br>So far so Borgesian, but there's a difference: Borges <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145560209" title="My review of Borges' Collected Fictions" rel="nofollow noopener">knows he's playing.</a> For Dick the questions are more serious. His major influence is noir, and his books are dark, and when he questions reality he's <i>seriously questioning reality.</i> He doesn't really have a guess. He was beset by hallucinations throughout his life. He believed for a while that he was the reincarnated prophet Elijah. He may have been schizophrenic. He was certainly a heavy drug user. There's anguish at the bottom of his writing. Borges thinks it's neat to wonder what's real. Dick thinks it's terrifying.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17897130964339159087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2192951063" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2192951063" />
    <a title="Manuel Antão" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28709846-manuel-ant-o"><img alt="Manuel Antão" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504271107p2/28709846.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2192951063?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manuel Antão" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manuel Antão" href="/user/show/28709846-manuel-ant-o">Manuel Antão</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780679736646" href="/book/show/590036.Ubik">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28709846-manuel-ant-o?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28709846-manuel-ant-o?shelf=2008">2008</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2192951063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3903602173176498037">If you're into stuff like this, <a href='https://manuelaantao.blogspot.pt/2017/11/dont-throw-baby-out-with-bath-water.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>you can read the full review.</a><br/><br/>Don't Throw the Baby Out With the Bath Water: "Ubik" by Philip K. Dick <br/><br/>"'I am Ubik. Before the universe was, I am. I made the suns. I made the worlds. I created the lives and the places they inhabit; I move them here, I put them there. They go as I say, they do as I tell them. I am the word and my name is never spoken, the name which no one knows. I am called Ubik but that is not my name. I am. I shall always be. ‘“<br/><br/> <br/>In “Ubik” by Philip</span>
  <span id="freeText3903602173176498037" style="display:none">If you're into stuff like this, <a href="https://manuelaantao.blogspot.pt/2017/11/dont-throw-baby-out-with-bath-water.html" rel="nofollow noopener">you can read the full review.</a><br /><br />Don't Throw the Baby Out With the Bath Water: "Ubik" by Philip K. Dick <br /><br />"'I am Ubik. Before the universe was, I am. I made the suns. I made the worlds. I created the lives and the places they inhabit; I move them here, I put them there. They go as I say, they do as I tell them. I am the word and my name is never spoken, the name which no one knows. I am called Ubik but that is not my name. I am. I shall always be. ‘“<br /><br /> <br />In “Ubik” by Philip K. Dick<br /> <br /> <br />This would feel like a meaningless read indeed if it wasn't, in fact, a very FUNNY one, full of a dry humor. In Ubik the characters are taken in such a subjective maze of crumbling reality, unexpected time-travelling and personal doubts, that it becomes a materialization of the absurdity of the human condition, in the form of an exhilarating fiction. If you are not into the humor of Kafka and Borges, it makes perfectly sense that you are not sensible to Dick's one. What makes Ubik a wonderful read still today? Dick didn't nail everything too tightly to the plot. The result may seem a potpourri but his worlds live and breathe. If he were writing now this book would make him a rebel and, given what he was like, would give most editors / publishers gray-hairs. It also begs the question (of others in the genre): Can you really do that?<br /> <br />I think the current fascination with Dick seems tied to the fact that most of his most popular books have dystopian or control themes. The other worldliness, or just around the corner-ness, of his stories, make it seem fictional, therefore enjoyable, yet also real and possible. I had been seeing a resurgence in sales of his books a couple of decades ago. This is just a speculative thought, but I wonder: If we had really been reading him for a spooky window into the future, then that means that the "seeds of the future dystopia" already started back then. Nixon had been around in Dick's time, but Reagan and the Republican nasties was their second coming. AI was only just poking its nose into things. 2000 was around the corner. Was Dick one of our clues to the future?<br /> <br /> <br />If you're into SF, read on.</span>

<div id="review_70237305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70237305" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70237305?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=spooky-powers">spooky-powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=100">100</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70237305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7086342783561562236">I don't know why but I always get a huge kick out of reading an older sci-fi story that was set in the near future, but it's a date I've lived through. In 2001, I'd just randomly shout, "Kubrick and Clarke were wrong,! We don't have bases on the moon! Those fools!" This is another one where Phil didn't exactly nail 1992 writing in 1969, but it's still a pretty good story.<br/><br/>In this 1992, there are people with psionic powers like telepathy or precognition that are used for industrial sabotage, and r</span>
  <span id="freeText7086342783561562236" style="display:none">I don't know why but I always get a huge kick out of reading an older sci-fi story that was set in the near future, but it's a date I've lived through. In 2001, I'd just randomly shout, "Kubrick and Clarke were wrong,! We don't have bases on the moon! Those fools!" This is another one where Phil didn't exactly nail 1992 writing in 1969, but it's still a pretty good story.<br /><br />In this 1992, there are people with psionic powers like telepathy or precognition that are used for industrial sabotage, and rival firms are hired to stop it. The dead can be kept in a half-life state and can have limited communication with the living. <br /><br />Joe Chip is a tester for Glen Runcitor's anti-psi security firm, and when a job with a team of Runcitor employees goes horribly wrong, Joe finds reality shifting around him and is soon unable to distinguish past from present and what's real from what isn't. The only constant thing are ads telling him to try the wonderful product Ubik.<br /><br />This is Philip K. doing his usual mind-bending thing, but this time instead of just questioning identity or memory, he's questioning the nature of reality itself. A little dated, but pretty good stuff with a lot of dark humor, which is something there isn't enough of in sci-fi.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7086342783561562236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/240534693?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marvin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marvin" href="/user/show/2160536-marvin">Marvin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780679736646" href="/book/show/590036.Ubik">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2160536-marvin?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240534693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14308990438359292013">This is one of Philip K. Dick's strangest novels. Those who have read his novels know that is saying a lot. But there were a few surprises for me. This is one of his wittiest novels. There are a lot of clever moments especially at the beginning. Yet sooner or later Dick will take you into the weird dimension and he does it with finesse. I do not have the patience to describe the plot. Even the Goodreads description at the top is lacking. But all the necessary ingredients... frustrated protagonis</span>
  <span id="freeText14308990438359292013" style="display:none">This is one of Philip K. Dick's strangest novels. Those who have read his novels know that is saying a lot. But there were a few surprises for me. This is one of his wittiest novels. There are a lot of clever moments especially at the beginning. Yet sooner or later Dick will take you into the weird dimension and he does it with finesse. I do not have the patience to describe the plot. Even the Goodreads description at the top is lacking. But all the necessary ingredients... frustrated protagonists, strange alternate realities, a taste of the mystic, etc...for a Dick novel is here and they come together nicely with one of his best and most cryptic endings. This would be a great introductory read for those not familiar with this great athor. In fact, I would say if you haven't read <i>Ubik</i>, you haven't read Dick.<br /><br />Sorry. Couldn't resist.<br /><br />Four and a half stars.</span>

<div id="review_2338225166" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2338225166" />
    <a title="Matthew Appleton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57003346-matthew-appleton"><img alt="Matthew Appleton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578773686p2/57003346.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2338225166?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Appleton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Appleton" href="/user/show/57003346-matthew-appleton">Matthew Appleton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780547572291" href="/book/show/12346742-ubik">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57003346-matthew-appleton?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57003346-matthew-appleton?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57003346-matthew-appleton?shelf=sf">sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57003346-matthew-appleton?shelf=american-literature">american-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2338225166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12025659443695564218">59th book of 2020. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1588182562i/29377618._SX540_.jpg' width='700' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'm going to carefully say I love <i>Philip K.</i> Dick. I'll say the writing isn't phenomenal, it's very cinematic, which I usually don't care for. Books excite me when they make me think, or they linger in my head, and Dick manages to do that, without the fancy writing. Though, I do like fancy language. I like the word fancy too. <br/><br/>This book, as expected, is a little mind-blowing. Returning to his wonderful, favourite theme: Reality. And moreover, what is reality? I can't say much wi</span>
  <span id="freeText12025659443695564218" style="display:none">59th book of 2020. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1588182562i/29377618._SX540_.jpg" width="700" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm going to carefully say I love <i>Philip K.</i> Dick. I'll say the writing isn't phenomenal, it's very cinematic, which I usually don't care for. Books excite me when they make me think, or they linger in my head, and Dick manages to do that, without the fancy writing. Though, I do like fancy language. I like the word fancy too. <br><br>This book, as expected, is a little mind-blowing. Returning to his wonderful, favourite theme: Reality. And moreover, what is reality? I can't say much without spoiling the many twist and turns this book takes you through, which also I means I can't scream out the excitement, confusion and (slight) fear, on finishing. The best way to sum it up is by using someone else's quote, Grossman's: <br><br><i>"a deeply unsettling existential horror story, a nightmare you'll never be sure you've woken up from"</i><br><br>Exactly how it feels. Fans of <i>The Crying of Lot 49</i> and the movie <i>Inception</i>, converge here. I'll wait for you to arrive, whilst pondering my own existence, and or, reality.</span>

But as I got into his style this easily became one of my favorite PKD novels. <br/><br/>The story is unique and is a combination of science fiction and mystery. <div id="review_2320079108" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2320079108" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2320079108?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=bb-b-2018">bb-b-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320079108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10943710222814356950"><b>2.5 Half-Life Stars</b><br/><br/><b>Buddy Read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8192509-gavin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gavin the Great</a> at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>BB&B</a></b><br/><br/><b>Ubik is a wonder, it is anything and everything you could ever need.</b> It can taste like fresh brewed coffee, or a nice hoppy beer, or be used as salad dressing. It can relieve a headache or stomach ache or clean household items. It slices and It dices with a never dulling edge, plus makes your hair shine like never before. It will help you sleep, stops perspiration, freshens breath and will uplift your breasts. <b>But wait there’s more…..</b><br/><br/>It i</span>
  <span id="freeText10943710222814356950" style="display:none"><b>2.5 Half-Life Stars</b><br /><br /><b>Buddy Read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8192509-gavin" rel="nofollow noopener">Gavin the Great</a> at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">BB&amp;B</a></b><br /><br /><b>Ubik is a wonder, it is anything and everything you could ever need.</b> It can taste like fresh brewed coffee, or a nice hoppy beer, or be used as salad dressing. It can relieve a headache or stomach ache or clean household items. It slices and It dices with a never dulling edge, plus makes your hair shine like never before. It will help you sleep, stops perspiration, freshens breath and will uplift your breasts. <b>But wait there’s more…..</b><br /><br />It is hard to read a Sci-Fi book from 1969 and not feel like it is dated especially since the far off future is 1992. Philip K. Dick (PKD) thought we’d make it a lot farther than we actually did technology wise with the flying cars and talking electronics but since 1992 is our past sometimes it is hard to get past the things that are so off for that time period.<br /><br />A few things that are pretty cool in this book is the actual world and some of the discoveries in it. Like when your loved one dies you don’t bury them anymore, you store them in a kind of Cryo-sleep and then go visit once a month of so and talk to them. Depending on the person they can stay in this state for 15-30 years before moving on to be reborn. The other thing is that all of your items of use in your apartment need money to work. The door requires 5 cents to open, the shower a quarter. I’m not sure what the appliances buy with the money they make maybe they are saving up for something really nice.<br /><br />The issue I had with this book besides being dated is that the plot was all over the place and there really wasn’t any resolution to a lot of the threads. I was really liking the story until the halfway point when it turned into a black and white episode of the twilight zone. Then it got a bit strange but I was still following along, however the ending was completely unsatisfying overall. <br /><br />I struggled with the character development as well. Most of them were pretty flat. Even Joe Chip the main character was underdeveloped. He is an always broke guy with the ability to measure someone’s psychic potential or gift. He brings the talent to his boss who figures out how to use them in a large corporation that pretty much is a futuristic security firm of sorts. The first half of the story is centered on this and that is the part I liked more. The second half, well I mentioned the Twilight Zone so enough said there.<br /><br />Other than that there is a group of characters. The best guy friend, the love interest Joe should have had but never made the move for, the other woman that stepped in and acquired Joe for her own. Everyone else is really a throw away character. It is also so weird to read about all the smoking. Like every character in the book was a smoker and some of the story totally revolved around cigarettes. Reading it in 2018 was just strange.<br /><br />I can see how far the Sci-Fi genre has come and how PKD threw down a good base to grow off of. <b>Still it was like watching a Movie from your childhood and seeing how it just didn’t hold up over time.</b> You can still appreciate it but you’ve grown since then so it just isn’t the same.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10943710222814356950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1718539873" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1718539873" />
    <a title="Brian " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30718608-brian"><img alt="Brian " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567218975p2/30718608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1718539873?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian " href="/user/show/30718608-brian">Brian </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/315939.Ubik">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30718608-brian?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30718608-brian?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30718608-brian?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1718539873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15986870927873044773"> I have one all-time favorite movie (aside from adaptions of Hamlet): The Matrix. I novelized this movie before writing my own novel (and am still processing). I asked Goodreads if they knew of any books like this movie, and I received two suggestions by P.K. Dick, “Ubik,” and “Do Androids Dream of Electric Sheep?” <br/><br/> For some time this year I left the “pleasures” of reading to pursue my dreams of writing. I set out a plan: read literary magazines and short stories, write literary stories and get </span>
  <span id="freeText15986870927873044773" style="display:none"> I have one all-time favorite movie (aside from adaptions of Hamlet): The Matrix. I novelized this movie before writing my own novel (and am still processing). I asked Goodreads if they knew of any books like this movie, and I received two suggestions by P.K. Dick, “Ubik,” and “Do Androids Dream of Electric Sheep?” <br /><br /> For some time this year I left the “pleasures” of reading to pursue my dreams of writing. I set out a plan: read literary magazines and short stories, write literary stories and get published, publish a bunch and get rapport, writes a novel and publish the novel with that rapport. So, that took my fire away. I turned my whole purpose of reading into a goal tainted by selfish ambition. I started to lose my fire to write fiction, even considered quitting altogether.<br /> <br /> And now I’ve read “Ubik,” by P.K. Dick.<br /><br /> I have a new rule now, just for me: Read the books that make you want to keep reading more books. I want to write for pleasure now, not to achieve some pompous goal to prove something to myself only to cry I have no more worlds to conquer like Alexander the Great. The joy and pleasure of the story fills that desire, that void. I do this when I sing too. When I sing and play guitar to impress others, I fail to perform well. When I do it to bring myself into that sanctuary of peace and pleasure, and emotional drifting, I sound good, and others feel the pleasure I try to bring to myself.<br /><br /> Sorry about all the autobiographical stuff here.<br /><br /> I’m happy and excited. I feel like a kid who opened a Christmas present, and the thing he finds came from something he made up in his dreams. I’ve been searching for this. It’s all I’ve wanted. P.K. Dick has strong storytelling capabilities. He takes you on a path with a multitude of turns. You think you know how this will play out, and then you don’t and you do again, and then you give up and feel suspense because “what’s going on?!” <br /><br /> This story sets complicated futuristic ideas and weaves a complex plot around those ideas. A war wages between psychics digging in minds for info. Anti-psychics have the power to block them. The two businesses war against each other like mob bosses. The good guy gets set up and trapped in a room with the world’s top quality talents, and a bomb explodes. Let the games begin! The world starts to regress. A dead man sends messages that the reader has died but the messenger still lives. People start decaying rapidly and shrink into tiny skulls and layers of flesh. <br /><br /> You have to read this one if you like Sci-Fi, especially if you liked the Matrix. I see how this may have strongly influenced the Wachowski’s. I also see how Dick may have influenced King in his DT Series.<br /><br /> I can’t wait to read more of his stuff! He keeps me wanting to read, and reminds me of my best reason to write fiction.<br /><br /> For a thorough and concise overview of the complexities of the story, I recommend our friend Cecily's review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/580647608?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15986870927873044773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_99859650" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99859650" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99859650?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780679736646" href="/book/show/590036.Ubik">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=speculative">speculative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99859650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5824781667106597925">The concept behind <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/590036.Ubik' title='Ubik by Philip K. Dick' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ubik</a> is as brilliant as any of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4764.Philip_K__Dick' title='Philip K. Dick' rel='nofollow noopener'>Philip K. Dick</a>'s ideas. <br/><br/>Glen Runciter is dead, or maybe he's not. All the people who work for him in his anti-paranormal "Prudence Organization" are dead, or maybe they're not. But even if they're dead (having been attacked by the big Kahuna of paranormal activity), they're being kept in half-life at a Swiss cryogenic facility where they may now be under attack from a soul predator who sucks the vitality out of their half-life, devouring them to </span>
  <span id="freeText5824781667106597925" style="display:none">The concept behind <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/590036.Ubik" title="Ubik by Philip K. Dick" rel="nofollow noopener">Ubik</a> is as brilliant as any of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4764.Philip_K__Dick" title="Philip K. Dick" rel="nofollow noopener">Philip K. Dick</a>'s ideas. <br /><br />Glen Runciter is dead, or maybe he's not. All the people who work for him in his anti-paranormal "Prudence Organization" are dead, or maybe they're not. But even if they're dead (having been attacked by the big Kahuna of paranormal activity), they're being kept in half-life at a Swiss cryogenic facility where they may now be under attack from a soul predator who sucks the vitality out of their half-life, devouring them to power his own half-life. Maybe. We find out the answer in the end. Or maybe not.<br /><br />This uncertainty is, of course, on purpose. The author is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4764.Philip_K__Dick" title="Philip K. Dick" rel="nofollow noopener">Philip K. Dick</a>, after all, and bending our minds was always one of his greatest talents.<br /><br />The problem for me, though, is that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/590036.Ubik" title="Ubik by Philip K. Dick" rel="nofollow noopener">Ubik</a>'s execution doesn't match the brilliance of the idea it's trying to express. It feels like a lesser episode of <i>The Twilight Zone</i>; one of those episodes that couldn't transcend the time of its making, so we're too aware of its post-Nuclear War, pre-Space Age placement. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/590036.Ubik" title="Ubik by Philip K. Dick" rel="nofollow noopener">Ubik</a>, like its <i>Twilight Zone</i> kin, is too dated, which isn't unique in the oeuvre of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4764.Philip_K__Dick" title="Philip K. Dick" rel="nofollow noopener">Dick</a>. Even <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7082.Do_Androids_Dream_of_Electric_Sheep_" title="Do Androids Dream of Electric Sheep? by Philip K. Dick" rel="nofollow noopener">Do Androids Dream of Electric Sheep</a> suffers the same fate, making it one of the rare occasions when many readers find themselves admiring the movie (<i>Blade Runner</i>) more than its source.<br /><br />I wanted to like this more, and I can imagine an updated film of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/590036.Ubik" title="Ubik by Philip K. Dick" rel="nofollow noopener">Ubik</a> (maybe directed by Christopher Nolan) knocking my flip-flops off, but the book was disappointing. What a bummer. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5824781667106597925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10165256-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340093730p2/10165256.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/734516237?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/10165256-penny">Penny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165256-penny?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165256-penny?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165256-penny?shelf=scifi-and-fantasy-club-bookshelf">scifi-and-fantasy-club-bookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165256-penny?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165256-penny?shelf=books-they-say-i-should-read">books-they-say-i-should-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165256-penny?shelf=highly-recommended">highly-recommended</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer734516237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17650895951113293512">This book is pure genius! Even when I was as confused as Joe Chip about what in the hell was really going on, I loved every second of it. The concept behind this novel is brilliant. We spend a great deal of it unsure of what is real and what isn't and some of the ideas Dick manages to throw in as the story progresses had me grinning and shaking my head at the crazy logic of it all.<br/><br/>One of my favourites was the question of whether or not you can out-random a guy who had precogs tell him your every</span>
  <span id="freeText17650895951113293512" style="display:none">This book is pure genius! Even when I was as confused as Joe Chip about what in the hell was really going on, I loved every second of it. The concept behind this novel is brilliant. We spend a great deal of it unsure of what is real and what isn't and some of the ideas Dick manages to throw in as the story progresses had me grinning and shaking my head at the crazy logic of it all.<br /><br />One of my favourites was the question of whether or not you can out-random a guy who had precogs tell him your every move weeks ago. It was reminiscent of conversations about free will back in undergraduate days when we were all philosophers. Is it really 'choice' or is it just a deterministic reaction of the synapses in your brain to external stimuli? <br /><br />I love the Ubik ads at the beginning of each chapter. The “adult cereal” one in particular. So funny :) <br /><br />I think the first time reading this book will always be special because you don't yet know what's actually going on and it's all a mystery that you unravel with the merry band of characters. However I suspect I'll get a lot out of re-reads of this one and I'm very much looking forward to that already. <br /><br />Top marks. First class. If you haven't read it, you really should. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17650895951113293512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wBaRMqW9aynJb6nkGZAxL/Wvo+pze3CyoissEMeoUBb+Kdeps6UTZuynL8IA6xwDVL0HoIQaN37u2sCIm8LMug==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RM8TLO3LcHUZo2GOYzcFCCIFG0IL0l+4CzkqMdV2MQ568FW3+9MIOjxr56h6TCgkgxe/CPyzGHRHyMapiRytog==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4764.Philip_K_Dick">About Philip K. Dick</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4764.Philip_K_Dick"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1264613853p3/4764.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/4764.Philip_K_Dick">Philip K. Dick
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
16,987
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6639458924231853110">Philip K. Dick was born in Chicago in 1928 and lived most of his life in California. In 1952, he began writing professionally and proceeded to write numerous novels and short-story collections. He won the Hugo Award for the best novel in 1962 for <i>The Man in the High Castle</i> and the John W. Campbell Memorial Award for best novel of the year in 1974 for <i>Flow My Tears, the Policeman Said</i>. Philip K. Di</span>
  <span id="freeText6639458924231853110" style="display:none">Philip K. Dick was born in Chicago in 1928 and lived most of his life in California. In 1952, he began writing professionally and proceeded to write numerous novels and short-story collections. He won the Hugo Award for the best novel in 1962 for <i>The Man in the High Castle</i> and the John W. Campbell Memorial Award for best novel of the year in 1974 for <i>Flow My Tears, the Policeman Said</i>. Philip K. Dick died on March 2, 1982, in Santa Ana, California, of heart failure following a stroke.<br /><br />In addition to 44 published novels, Dick wrote approximately 121 short stories, most of which appeared in science fiction magazines during his lifetime. Although Dick spent most of his career as a writer in near-poverty, ten of his stories have been adapted into popular films since his death, including <i>Blade Runner, Total Recall, A Scanner Darkly, Minority Report, Paycheck, Next, Screamers</i>, and <i>The Adjustment Bureau</i>. In 2005, Time magazine named <i>Ubik</i> one of the one hundred greatest English-language novels published since 1923. In 2007, Dick became the first science fiction writer to be included in The Library of America series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6639458924231853110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
